    <script type="text/javascript" nonce="02e3eda28d4f409a881ee5576ef88ce5">

        function getParameter(parameterName) {
            let result = null,
                tmp = [];
            location.search
                .substr(1)
                .split("&")
                .forEach(function (item) {
                    tmp = item.split("=");
                    if (tmp[0] === parameterName) result = tmp[1];
                });
            return result;
        }

        var SeamlessAccessService = {
            spUrl: "/action/ssostart",
            returnURL: window.location.href,
            my_context: 'seamlessaccess.org',
            queryParamsDelimiter: encodeURIComponent('?'),

            getWAYFLessUrl: function (entityId) {
                let redirectURL = getParameter('redirectUri');
                if(redirectURL == null){
                    redirectURL = encodeURIComponent(this.returnURL);
                }
                if(redirectURL.indexOf('saml_referrer') < 0){
                    redirectURL += encodeURIComponent(((redirectURL.indexOf(this.queryParamsDelimiter) !== -1) ? '&' : '?') + 'saml_referrer');
                }
                return this.spUrl + "?idp=" + encodeURIComponent(entityId)
                    + "&redirectUri=" + redirectURL;
            },
            retrieveEntity: function () {
                var self = this;
                var ps = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    ps.entities(self.my_context)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            // get the results
                            var results = res.data;
                            return resolve(results);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            reject('retrieve entity error: ' + err);
                        });
                });
            },
            updateEntity: function (entitydata) {
                var self = this;
                var ps = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                var jsonObj = {};
                try {
                    //try to parse it, if it is a json string
                    jsonObj = JSON.parse(entitydata.val());
                } catch (e) {
                    jsonObj = entitydata;
                }
                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    ps.update(self.my_context, jsonObj)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            // Process the results
                            var ssoInstitutions = res.data;
                            return resolve(ssoInstitutions);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            console.log('failed to update the local storage duo to: ' + err);
                            reject(err);
                        });
                })
            },
            removeEntity: function (entityId) {
                var self = this;
                var persistService = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                return new Promise(function (resolve) {
                    persistService.remove(self.my_context, entityId)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            return resolve(res);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            console.log('failed to remove from local storage duo to: ' + err);
                        });
                })
            },
            getAccessibleEntityStatus: function (doi, entityId, entityTitle) {
                return new Promise(function (resolve) {
                    $.ajax({
                        type: 'POST',
                        url: '/action/seamlessAccess',
                        accept: {
                            text: "application/json"
                        },
                        data: {doi: doi, entityid: entityId, entityTitle: entityTitle, eventGroupKey: '5945fc48-5807-44d7-a229-a375725b390e'}

                    }).done(function (status) {
                        return resolve(status);
                    });
                });
            },
            getEntitiesWithAllInfo: function (doi) {
                let self = this,
                    arrayOfPromises = [];
                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    self.retrieveEntity().then(function (res) {
                        let allSsoInstitutions = res;
                        for (let i in allSsoInstitutions) {
                            let ssoInstitution = allSsoInstitutions[i];
                            arrayOfPromises.push(new Promise(function (resolve) {
                                self.getAccessibleEntityStatus(doi, ssoInstitution.entity.entityID, ssoInstitution.entity.title)
                                    .then(function (entityStatus) {
                                        resolve({
                                            entityID: ssoInstitution.entity.entityID,
                                            entityTitle: ssoInstitution.entity.title,
                                            entityStatusObj: entityStatus,
                                            entitySsoUrl: self.getWAYFLessUrl(ssoInstitution.entity.entityID)
                                        });
                                    }, function (err) {
                                        console.log('failed to get the entity status: ' + err);
                                    });
                            }));
                        }
                        Promise.all(arrayOfPromises)
                            .then(function (finalResponse) {
                                resolve(finalResponse);
                            });

                    }).catch(function (err) {
                        reject(err);
                    })
                });
            }
        };

        window.addEventListener('load', function () {
            document.querySelectorAll(".sso-institution").forEach(function (institution) {
                var entityId = institution.getAttribute('data-entityid');
                var entityName = institution.getAttribute('data-name');
                var entitydata = {
                    entityID: entityId,
                    title: entityName
                };
                institution.addEventListener("click", function (e) {
                    e.preventDefault();
                    var self = this;
                    SeamlessAccessService.updateEntity(entitydata).then(function (res) {
                        console.log(res);
                        window.location.href = self.href;
                    }).catch(function (err){
                        window.location.href = self.href;
                    });
                });
            });
        });

    </script>

   <div class="abstract-group ">
      <section class="article-section article-section__abstract" lang="en" data-lang="en" lang-name="English" id="section-1-en">
         <h2 id="d9131749" class="article-section__header section__title main abstractlang_en main">Abstract</h2>
         <div class="article-section__content en main">
            
            <p>As a typical tunnel oxide, Na<sub>0.44</sub>MnO<sub>2</sub> features excellent electrochemical performance and outstanding structural stability, making it a promising cathode for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs). However, it suffers from undesirable challenges such as surface residual alkali, multiple voltage plateaus, and low initial charge specific capacity. Herein, an internal and external synergistic modulation strategy is adopted by replacing part of the Mn with Ti to optimize the bulk phase and construct a Ti-containing epitaxial stabilization layer, resulting in reduced surface residual alkali, excellent Na<sup>+</sup> transport kinetics and improved water/air stability. Specifically, the Na<sub>0.44</sub>Mn<sub>0.85</sub>Ti<sub>0.15</sub>O<sub>2</sub> using water-soluble carboxymethyl cellulose as a binder can realize a capacity retention rate of 94.30% after 1,000 cycles at 2C, and excellent stability is further verified in kilogram large-up applications. In addition, taking advantage of the rich Na content in Prussian blue analog (PBA), PBA-Na<sub>0.44</sub>Mn<sub>1-x</sub>Ti<sub>x</sub>O<sub>2</sub> composites are designed to compensate for the insufficient Na in the tunnel oxide and are matched with hard carbon to achieve the preparation of coin full cell and 18650 cylindrical battery with satisfactory electrochemical performance. This work enables the application of tunnel oxides cathode for SIBs in 18650 cylindrical batteries for the first time and promotes the commercialization of SIBs.</p>
            </div>
      </section>
   </div>
   <div class="pb-dropzone" data-pb-dropzone="below-abstract-group"><!-- Empty dropzone --></div>
   
   <section class="article-section article-section__full">
      <section class="article-section__content" id="adma202407994-sec-0010">
         
         <h2 class="article-section__title section__title section1" id="adma202407994-sec-0010-title">1 Introduction</h2>
         
         <p>Efficient and sustainable energy storage systems are urgently needed in response to the growing energy crisis and environmental concerns.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202407994-bib-0001" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202407994-bib-0001_R_d9131741e614" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 1 - Nat. Commun. Adv. Energy Mater.">1</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Due to the high energy density, lithium-ion batteries (LIBs) have attracted much attention as one of the most promising candidates for energy storage systems. However, the scarcity and extremely uneven global distribution of lithium resources hinder its application in large-scale energy storage.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202407994-bib-0002" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202407994-bib-0002_R_d9131741e619" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 2 - Nat. Commun. Carbon Neutraliz. Chem. Rec. Carbon Energy">2</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) with the same “rocking chair” mechanism as LIBs were promising to blossom in the batteries area because of the abundant reserves and global distribution of sodium resources.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202407994-bib-0003" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202407994-bib-0003_R_d9131741e624" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 3 - Chinese Chem. Lett. Sci. Rep. Adv. Energy Mater.">3</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Normally, the cathodes of SIBs are categorized into four main types, including polyanionic compounds (PA), Prussian blue analogs (PBAs), organic compounds, and sodium transition metal oxides (NaTMO<sub>2</sub>).<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202407994-bib-0004" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202407994-bib-0004_R_d9131741e632" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 4 - Nano Energy Angew. Chem. Int. Ed. Adv. Mater.">4</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Drawing on the successful application of lithium transition metal oxides (LiTMO<sub>2</sub>), it is believed that NaTMO<sub>2</sub> can learn from the design principle of LiTMO<sub>2</sub>, which has attracted much research interest.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202407994-bib-0005" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202407994-bib-0005_R_d9131741e644" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 5 - Int. J. Energy Res. Adv. Funct. Mater. Chem. Soc. Rev. Nat. Commun. Angew. Chem. Int. Ed.">5</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The tunnel oxide material represented by Na<sub>0.44</sub>MnO<sub>2</sub> is one of the most typical NaTMO<sub>2</sub> with unique S-shaped channels, which facilitates the rapid insertion and extraction of Na<sup>+</sup> and exhibits excellent air/water stability.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202407994-bib-0006" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202407994-bib-0006_R_d9131741e658" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 6 - Nat. Commun. Energy Environ. Mater. Chem. Electro. Chem. Nano Energy">6</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup></p>
         
         <p>However, Na<sub>0.44</sub>MnO<sub>2</sub> is still plagued by the following problems<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202407994-bib-0007" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202407994-bib-0007_R_d9131741e669" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 7 - Sci. China Chem. Adv. Mater. ACS Appl. Mater. Interfaces InfoMat">7</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup>: 1) Na<sup>+</sup>/H<sup>+</sup> ion exchange leads to high surface residual alkali, which causes gelation of the cathode slurry and impairs the electrochemical performance; 2) Multiple voltage plateaus in the charge/discharge profiles exerts adverse effects on the kinetic behavior; 3) The low sodium stoichiometry ratio of Na<sub>0.44</sub>MnO<sub>2</sub> is not suitable for full cell assembly when matched with hard carbon, so a strategy is required to compensate for the sodium lost during solid electrolyte interphase (SEI) layer formation. To overcome the above challenges, various modification strategies were proposed. For example, 1) Coating strategies are used to reduce surface alkali<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202407994-bib-0008" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202407994-bib-0008_R_d9131741e683" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 8 - Adv. Energy Mater. Nat. Commun. Adv. Funct. Mater.">8</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup>; 2) Doping elements are performed&nbsp;to regulate the electrochemical behaviors during the charge/discharge process<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202407994-bib-0009" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202407994-bib-0009_R_d9131741e689" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 9 - Adv. Sci. J. Power Sources Adv. Funct. Mater.">9</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup>; 3) Pre-sodiation for the hard carbon anode is applied to compensate for the sodium consumed in forming SEI film.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202407994-bib-0010" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202407994-bib-0010_R_d9131741e694" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 10 - Nat. Commun.">10</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> However, these modification strategies are mainly focused on the solution of a single problem and rarely address the above problems simultaneously. Therefore, to realize the practical application of Na<sub>0.44</sub>MnO<sub>2</sub>, it is necessary to develop a simple method to improve its overall performance.</p>
         
         <p>In this work, an internal and external strengthening strategy by Ti-substituted was proposed to reduce the material surface alkali, modulate the electrochemical behaviors and further improve the water resistance of the Na<sub>0.44</sub>MnO<sub>2</sub>. It is worth noting that the Ti-substituted materials exhibit ultra-high cycle stability not only in the conventional PVDF/NMP (polyvinylidene fluoride as a binder and N-methyl pyrrolidone as a solvent denoted as PVDF/NMP) system but also in the CMC/H<sub>2</sub>O (carboxymethyl cellulose as a binder and deionized water as a solvent denoted as CMC/H<sub>2</sub>O) system. In addition, in situ X-ray diffraction (XRD) demonstrates the excellent structural stability of the Ti-substituted samples during charging and discharging, and deep-etched X-ray photoelectron spectroscopy (XPS) also further confirms the presence of a titanium epitaxial layer on the surface, which enhances the cycling stability of the electrodes. Density Functional Theory (DFT) calculations were performed to elucidate the mechanism of the electronic structure, further demonstrating the excellent hydrophobicity of the titanium-substituted cathode material. Moreover, the preparation of a large batch of Na<sub>0.44</sub>Mn<sub>0.85</sub>Ti<sub>0.15</sub>O<sub>2</sub> material was carried out using industrial-grade raw materials. When compared to the electrochemical performance of small laboratory batches, it still exhibits excellent rate performance and cycle stability. The capacity retention of the prepared industrial-grade Na<sub>0.44</sub>Mn<sub>0.85</sub>Ti<sub>0.15</sub>O<sub>2</sub> electrode (CMC/H<sub>2</sub>O) is up to 89.70% after 500 cycles at 2C. In addition, taking advantage of the sodium-rich nature of Prussian blue analog (PBA),<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202407994-bib-0011" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202407994-bib-0011_R_d9131741e734" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 11 - Small Angew. Chem. Int. Ed. Nat. Commun.">11</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> a novel sodium-compensating strategy of physically mixing sodium-rich PBA with the Na<sub>0.44</sub>Mn<sub>0.85</sub>Ti<sub>0.15</sub>O<sub>2</sub> materials was proposed here to prepare composite structures with synergistic effects that improve their initial coulombic efficiency. The prepared PBA-Na<sub>0.44</sub>Mn<sub>0.85</sub>Ti<sub>0.15</sub>O<sub>2</sub> composite was used as the cathode and assembled with the hard carbon anode for the coin full cell and the 18650 cylindrical battery, which realized the scale-up of tunnel oxide cathodes from the laboratory to industrial-scale production for the first time, providing an important reference for the practical application of tunnel oxide cathodes in SIBs.</p>
         </section>
      <section class="article-section__content" id="adma202407994-sec-0020">
         
         <h2 class="article-section__title section__title section1" id="adma202407994-sec-0020-title">2 Results and Discussion</h2>
         
         <p>For the Mn in the Na<sub>0.44</sub>MnO<sub>2</sub>, its 3d electronic orbitals are divided into the e<sub>g</sub> and t<sub>2g</sub>, where the t<sub>2g</sub> orbitals of Mn<sup>4+</sup> are fully occupied and the e<sub>g</sub> orbitals are unoccupied, enabling the formation of the ideal MnO<sub>6</sub> octahedral structure.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202407994-bib-0004" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202407994-bib-0004_R_d9131741e782" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 4 - Nano Energy Angew. Chem. Int. Ed. Adv. Mater.">4</a>, <a href="#adma202407994-bib-0012" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202407994-bib-0012_R_d9131741e782" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 12 - Composites, Part B">12</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> In contrast, the e<sub>g</sub> orbital of Mn<sup>3+</sup> splits into two orbitals near the Fermi energy level, resulting in the Jahn-Teller distortion and leading to poor cycling performance.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202407994-bib-0013" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202407994-bib-0013_R_d9131741e792" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 13 - Energy Environ. Sci.">13</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> According to the previous reports, Ti has a similar ionic radius to Mn and is at a different Fermi level to Mn, and replacing part of the Mn in Na<sub>0.44</sub>MnO<sub>2</sub> with Ti can lead to weak TM-O orbital hybridization.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202407994-bib-0014" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202407994-bib-0014_R_d9131741e802" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 14 - Energy Storage Mater.">14</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> To prove this point, the partial density of states (pDOS) of the Na<sub>0.44</sub>MnO<sub>2</sub> and Na<sub>0.44</sub>Mn<sub>0.85</sub>Ti<sub>0.15</sub>O<sub>2</sub> was calculated and shown in <b>Figures</b> <a href="#adma202407994-fig-0001">1a,b</a>, the high-energy e<sub>g</sub> orbitals of Na<sub>0.44</sub>MnO<sub>2</sub> are split into two groups, which are located above and below the Fermi level, indicating that the existence of an active Jahn-Teller effect of Mn<sup>3+</sup> ions. In contrast, the e<sub>g</sub> orbitals of Mn in Na<sub>0.44</sub>Mn<sub>0.85</sub>Ti<sub>0.15</sub>O<sub>2</sub> are not split, suggesting that the Mn in the Na<sub>0.44</sub>Mn<sub>0.85</sub>Ti<sub>0.15</sub>O<sub>2</sub> is not involved in the Jahn-Teller effect. The results show that Ti substitution effectively inhibits the harmful Jahn-Teller effect. In addition, The Mn 3d orbitals of the Na<sub>0.44</sub>MnO<sub>2</sub> have a band gap of 3.56&nbsp;eV, whereas the Mn 3d orbitals of Na<sub>0.44</sub>Mn<sub>0.85</sub>Ti<sub>0.15</sub>O<sub>2</sub> have no band gap, indicating that the introduction of Ti improves the electronic conductivity. Furthermore, the increased overlap regions of the Mn (3d)-O (2p) orbitals in Na<sub>0.44</sub>Mn<sub>0.85</sub>Ti<sub>0.15</sub>O<sub>2</sub> demonstrated that the Ti substitution can enhance the energy of the Mn─O bond, which is favorable for the structural stability.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202407994-bib-0015" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202407994-bib-0015_R_d9131741e876" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 15 - Nat. Commun. Adv. Mater. Nat. Commun. J. Am. Chem. Soc.">15</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup></p>
         
         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="adma202407994-fig-0001"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/c0ed7d8d-d962-487c-90bb-a9d871c3b05a/adma202407994-fig-0001-m.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/c0ed7d8d-d962-487c-90bb-a9d871c3b05a/adma202407994-fig-0001-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/f30f0131-2b8c-4cc8-aadf-e5f6ffdeface/adma202407994-fig-0001-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/c0ed7d8d-d962-487c-90bb-a9d871c3b05a/adma202407994-fig-0001-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                  <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 1<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=adma202407994-fig-0001&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fadma.202407994" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                  </div>
                  <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">Structure of Na<sub>0.44</sub>Mn<sub>1-x</sub>Ti<sub>x</sub>O<sub>2</sub> (x&nbsp;=&nbsp;0, 0.05, 0.10, 0.15, 0.20). a) pDOS of Na<sub>0.44</sub>MnO<sub>2</sub>. b) pDOS of Na<sub>0.44</sub>Mn<sub>0.85</sub>Ti<sub>0.15</sub>O<sub>2</sub>. c) XRD patterns and partial views of Na<sub>0.44</sub>Mn<sub>1-x</sub>Ti<sub>x</sub>O<sub>2</sub>. d) Schematic crystal structure of Na<sub>0.44</sub>Mn<sub>1-x</sub>Ti<sub>x</sub>O<sub>2</sub>. e–i) SEM images of Na<sub>0.44</sub>Mn<sub>1-x</sub>Ti<sub>x</sub>O<sub>2</sub>. j) TEM image of Na<sub>0.44</sub>Mn<sub>0.85</sub>Ti<sub>0.15</sub>O<sub>2</sub>. k–o) Contact angle test results of Na<sub>0.44</sub>Mn<sub>1-x</sub>Ti<sub>x</sub>O<sub>2</sub>. p) Variation of lattice parameters <i>a</i>, <i>b</i>, and <i>c</i> for Na<sub>0.44</sub>Mn<sub>1-x</sub>Ti<sub>x</sub>O<sub>2</sub>. q) Variation of PH and change in contact angle of Na<sub>0.44</sub>Mn<sub>1-x</sub>Ti<sub>x</sub>O<sub>2</sub>.</div>
               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
         <p>The above results indicate that the partial substitution of Mn by Ti in Na<sub>0.44</sub>MnO<sub>2</sub> has a positive effect on the optimization of the structure, and inspired by this, a series of Na<sub>0.44</sub>Mn<sub>1-x</sub>Ti<sub>x</sub>O<sub>2</sub> (x&nbsp;=&nbsp;0.05, 0.10, 0.15, 0.20) materials were prepared by conventional high-temperature solid phase sintering method. From the powder X-ray diffraction (XRD) in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adma202407994-fig-0001">1c</a>, it can be seen that all the peaks of Na<sub>0.44</sub>Mn<sub>1-x</sub>Ti<sub>x</sub>O<sub>2</sub> materials display typical tunnel structure peaks with the <i>Pbam</i> space group (JCPDS No.27-0750).<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202407994-bib-0016" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202407994-bib-0016_R_d9131741e1018" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 16 - InfoMat">16</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> With the increase of titanium content, the XRD patterns show that the characteristic diffraction peaks of tunnel structure only very slightly shift to low angles. Meanwhile, it is worth noting that the splitting of the (350) peak also gradually disappears (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S1</a>, Supporting Information). As a typical tunnel oxide, the crystal structure of Na<sub>0.44</sub>Mn<sub>1-x</sub>Ti<sub>x</sub>O<sub>2</sub> contains three sodium sites and five manganese sites (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adma202407994-fig-0001">1d</a>) with the Mn (2) and Mn (5) are occupied by Mn<sup>3+</sup>, whereas the Mn (1), Mn (3) and Mn (4) are occupied by Mn<sup>4+</sup>, the Na (1) atom occupying a separate 1D tunnel, the Na (2) and Na (3) atoms at the “S” cavity sites.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202407994-bib-0017" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202407994-bib-0017_R_d9131741e1043" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 17 - Adv. Energy Mater.">17</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The existence of similarity ensures that Ti<sup>4+</sup> will not affect the original tunnel structure when replacing Mn in the TM layer. In addition, we analyzed the variation of lattice parameters, crystal spacing, surface alkali, and hydrophobicity of Na<sub>0.44</sub>Mn<sub>1-x</sub>Ti<sub>x</sub>O<sub>2</sub> (Figures&nbsp;<a href="#adma202407994-fig-0001">1e-q</a>; Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S2–S7</a>, and Table <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S1,S2</a>, Supporting Information). We performed scanning electron microscopy (SEM) measurements of Na<sub>0.44</sub>Mn<sub>1-x</sub>Ti<sub>x</sub>O<sub>2</sub> at different magnifications the Na<sub>0.44</sub>Mn<sub>1-x</sub>Ti<sub>x</sub>O<sub>2</sub> (x&nbsp;=&nbsp;0, 0.05, 0.10, 0.15, 0.20) materials (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adma202407994-fig-0001">1e–i</a> and Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S2</a>, Supporting Information), which shows a typical tunnel structure with high crystallinity. The results of the energy dispersive spectroscopy (EDS) images of the Na<sub>0.44</sub>Mn<sub>1-x</sub>Ti<sub>x</sub>O<sub>2</sub> materials display the presence of the elements Na, Mn, Ti, and O, which are uniformly distributed (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S3</a>, Supporting Information). Rietveld refinement of the powder XRD (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adma202407994-fig-0001">1p</a>; Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S4</a>, Supporting Information) shows that the lattice parameters of <i>a</i>, <i>b</i>, and <i>c</i> increase with the gradual increase in titanium content. This may be due to the doping of Ti<sup>4+</sup> increasing the bond length of Na─O and the d-spacing of the Na layer. Transmission electron microscopy (TEM) images of Na<sub>0.44</sub>Mn<sub>0.95</sub>Ti<sub>0.05</sub>O<sub>2</sub> and Na<sub>0.44</sub>Mn<sub>0.85</sub>Ti<sub>0.15</sub>O<sub>2</sub> are shown in Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S5</a> (Supporting Information) and Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adma202407994-fig-0001">1j</a>, respectively, with the 0.459&nbsp;nm d-spacing and the 0.454&nbsp;nm d-spacing belong to the (200) of the tunnel structure, respectively. Meanwhile, there is the Ti-containing epitaxial layer crystal lattice on the surface of Na<sub>0.44</sub>Mn<sub>0.85</sub>Ti<sub>0.15</sub>O<sub>2</sub>. To further prove the existence and role of the surface layer, pH and contact angle of the Na<sub>0.44</sub>Mn<sub>1-x</sub>Ti<sub>x</sub>O<sub>2</sub> materials were surveyed. The results of the pH test are shown in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adma202407994-fig-0001">1q</a>, Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S6</a>, and Table <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S1</a> (Supporting Information), which clearly show that there is a significant decrease in the pH value with the gradual increase in Ti content. It is worth mentioning that the decrease is not obvious when the titanium content is 0.05, but when the titanium content is increased to 0.15, the pH value starts to drop sharply from 11.00 to 10.63. The existence of the Ti-containing epitaxial layer reduces residual alkali on the surface of the material, thereby lowering the pH. Furthermore, it also acts as a hydrophobic layer, effectively preventing water molecules from damaging the material. The results of the contact angle measurement of Na<sub>0.44</sub>Mn<sub>1-x</sub>Ti<sub>x</sub>O<sub>2</sub> are shown in Figures&nbsp;<a href="#adma202407994-fig-0001">1k–o</a>, Figure <a href="#adma202407994-fig-0001">1q</a> and Table <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S2</a> (Supporting Information), which indicate that the contact angle on the surface of the titanium-doped samples increases from 97.84° to 124.68°. As shown in Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S7</a> (Supporting Information), the Zeta potential (ζ) becomes more negative with increasing Ti content, indicating that the material is more stable in water.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202407994-bib-0018" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202407994-bib-0018_R_d9131741e1191" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 18 - Chin. Chem. Lett. Adv. Sustainable Syst. Electrochim. Acta">18</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup></p>
         
         <p>As shown in <b>Figure</b> <a href="#adma202407994-fig-0002">2</a>, the electrochemical performance of the Na<sub>0.44</sub>Mn<sub>1-x</sub>Ti<sub>x</sub>O<sub>2</sub> (x&nbsp;=&nbsp;0, 0.05, 0.10, 0.15, 0.20) with PVDF/NMP system was thoroughly investigated. The galvanostatic charge/discharge (GCD) curves of Na<sub>0.44</sub>Mn<sub>1-x</sub>Ti<sub>x</sub>O<sub>2</sub> for the first five cycles at 0.1C are shown in Figures&nbsp;<a href="#adma202407994-fig-0002">2a–e</a>, where the existence of six different plateaus corresponding to the Na<sup>+</sup>/vacancy ordering. Interestingly, the charge/discharge plateaus are gradually smoothed with the increasing Ti content, showing the effect of Ti substitution on Na<sup>+</sup>/vacancy ordering.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202407994-bib-0019" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202407994-bib-0019_R_d9131741e1228" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 19 - Nat. Commun. Small">19</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> In addition, as shown in Figures&nbsp;<a href="#adma202407994-fig-0002">2f–j</a> and Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S8</a> (Supporting Information), when the Ti doping content is up to 0.05, the Na<sub>0.44</sub>Mn<sub>0.95</sub>Ti<sub>0.05</sub>O<sub>2</sub> delivers superior rate performance, resulting from the fact that the introduction of Ti ions increases the crystal volume and improves the migration rate of Na<sup>+</sup> in the material. However, if the excess electrochemically inactive Ti is doped, the ratio of active Mn decreases accordingly, resulting in reduced rate performance. Meanwhile, the cyclic voltammetry (CV) measurements were conducted at different scan rates to further investigate the electrochemical behavior and sodium storage properties of Na<sub>0.44</sub>Mn<sub>1-x</sub>Ti<sub>x</sub>O<sub>2</sub>. As shown in Figures&nbsp;<a href="#adma202407994-fig-0002">2k–o</a>, the CV curves of Na<sub>0.44</sub>Mn<sub>1-x</sub>Ti<sub>x</sub>O<sub>2</sub> exhibit smoother curves with the increase of Ti content, which are consistent with the GCD curves, further indicating the inhibition effect for the Na<sup>+</sup>/vacancy ordering of the Ti substitution. According to the equation of <i>i&nbsp;=&nbsp;av<sup>b</sup></i> (where <i>i</i> is the current density and <i>v</i> is the scanning rate), the value of parameter <i>b</i>, which reflects the Na<sup>+</sup> storage mechanism of Na<sub>0.44</sub>Mn<sub>1-x</sub>Ti<sub>x</sub>O<sub>2</sub> can be calculated as 0.855, 0.850, 0.935, 0.939, and 0.896 (Figures <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S9,S10</a>, Supporting Information), suggesting that the capacitive Na<sup>+</sup> storage mechanism of the Na<sub>0.44</sub>Mn<sub>1-x</sub>Ti<sub>x</sub>O<sub>2</sub> electrodes is predominant. What's more, the Na<sup>+</sup> kinetic properties of Na<sub>0.44</sub>Mn<sub>1-x</sub>Ti<sub>x</sub>O<sub>2</sub> were surveyed by the galvanostatic intermittent titration technique (GITT). As shown in Figures <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S11,S12</a> (Supporting Information), the Na<sub>0.44</sub>Mn<sub>0.95</sub>Ti<sub>0.05</sub>O<sub>2</sub> shows good kinetic properties with minimal ohmic and voltage polarization, which benefits the rate performance and cycle stability.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202407994-bib-0020" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202407994-bib-0020_R_d9131741e1331" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 20 - Adv. Mater.">20</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The kinetic properties of Na<sub>0.44</sub>Mn<sub>1-x</sub>Ti<sub>x</sub>O<sub>2</sub> are also related to the charge transfer resistance. Electrochemical impedance spectroscopy (EIS) measurements in Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S13</a> (Supporting Information) show that the Na<sub>0.44</sub>Mn<sub>0.95</sub>Ti<sub>0.05</sub>O<sub>2</sub> displays the lowest charge transfer resistance before and after cycling, indicating optimal conductivity and fast kinetics. It is well known that cycle stability is one of the most important indicators of whether cathode materials can be used in practice. Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adma202407994-fig-0002">2p</a> shows that the Na<sub>0.44</sub>Mn<sub>0.95</sub>Ti<sub>0.05</sub>O<sub>2</sub> possesses the optimum cycle performance with the capacity retention rate is 85.50% after 650 cycles at 2C, which is higher than the counterparts with different Ti contents such as Na<sub>0.44</sub>MnO<sub>2</sub> (75.85%), Na<sub>0.44</sub>Mn<sub>0.9</sub>Ti<sub>0.1</sub>O<sub>2</sub> (85.10%), Na<sub>0.44</sub>Mn<sub>0.85</sub>Ti<sub>0.15</sub>O<sub>2</sub> (82.88%), Na<sub>0.44</sub>Mn<sub>0.8</sub>Ti<sub>0.2</sub>O<sub>2</sub> (82.50%). In the practical application of SIBs, the variation in operating temperature should be considered. Therefore, the cycle stability at high temperatures is extremely important.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202407994-bib-0021" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202407994-bib-0021_R_d9131741e1399" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 21 - Adv. Funct. Mater.">21</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> As shown in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adma202407994-fig-0002">2q</a> and Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S14</a> (Supporting Information), Na<sub>0.44</sub>Mn<sub>0.95</sub>Ti<sub>0.05</sub>O<sub>2</sub> shows a higher specific capacity and excellent rate performance at 55&nbsp;°C, which may be due to the enhanced kinetics of Na<sup>+</sup> and the improved electrochemical redox at high temperatures.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202407994-bib-0022" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202407994-bib-0022_R_d9131741e1422" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 22 - Adv. Mater.">22</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> In addition, after the rate performance test, Na<sub>0.44</sub>Mn<sub>0.95</sub>Ti<sub>0.05</sub>O<sub>2</sub> still shows 86.96% capacity retention after 300 cycles at 2C, demonstrating its high-temperature stability.</p>

            <figure class="figure" id="adma202407994-fig-0002"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/b5bf0e3e-82c1-431b-acb3-65bf5f241b7e/adma202407994-fig-0002-m.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/b5bf0e3e-82c1-431b-acb3-65bf5f241b7e/adma202407994-fig-0002-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/e3951848-f302-4b9f-b468-513acd9c42cb/adma202407994-fig-0002-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/b5bf0e3e-82c1-431b-acb3-65bf5f241b7e/adma202407994-fig-0002-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                  <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 2<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=adma202407994-fig-0002&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fadma.202407994" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>

               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
         <p>To gain insight into the structural stability of the Na<sub>0.44</sub>MnO<sub>2</sub> and Na<sub>0.44</sub>Mn<sub>0.95</sub>Ti<sub>0.05</sub>O<sub>2</sub> during the intercalation and extraction, in situ XRD was used to monitor the structural evolution during the initial charging and discharging process (<b>Figures</b> <a href="#adma202407994-fig-0003">3a,b</a>; Figures <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S15,S16</a>, Supporting Information), which reveals that the (130), (140), (200), and (350) characteristic peaks of the Na<sub>0.44</sub>Mn<sub>0.95</sub>Ti<sub>0.05</sub>O<sub>2</sub> are gradually shifted to higher angles, corresponding to the lattice contraction of Na<sub>0.44</sub>Mn<sub>0.95</sub>Ti<sub>0.05</sub>O<sub>2</sub> due to Na<sup>+</sup> extraction.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202407994-bib-0023" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202407994-bib-0023_R_d9131741e1554" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 23 - ACS Appl. Mater. Interfaces">23</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> In addition, the (350) peak splits during the charging process, giving rise to a new (0 10 0) peak, which disappears during the subsequent discharging process.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202407994-bib-0024" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202407994-bib-0024_R_d9131741e1559" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 24 - Chem. Eng. J.">24</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> And the other characteristic peaks also return to their original position during the sodiation process. Compared with Na<sub>0.44</sub>Mn<sub>0.95</sub>Ti<sub>0.05</sub>O<sub>2</sub>, the new peak (010 0) separated from the (350) peak by Na<sub>0.44</sub>MnO<sub>2</sub> produces a greater shift toward a higher angle, which demonstrates the excellent structural stability of the Na<sub>0.44</sub>Mn<sub>0.95</sub>Ti<sub>0.05</sub>O<sub>2</sub> during the charge/discharge process. The electronic states and surface chemistry of Na<sub>0.44</sub>Mn<sub>0.95</sub>Ti<sub>0.05</sub>O<sub>2</sub> were analyzed by the deep etch XPS (Figures&nbsp;<a href="#adma202407994-fig-0003">3c–h</a>; Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S17</a>, Supporting Information). The deep etch XPS spectra of Mn 2p in Figures&nbsp;<a href="#adma202407994-fig-0003">3c,f</a> shows two peak doublets of Mn<sup>3+</sup> (654.2 and 642.9&nbsp;eV) and Mn<sup>4+</sup> (653.1 and 641.6&nbsp;eV), suggesting the coexistence of the Mn<sup>3+</sup> and Mn<sup>4+</sup> in the Na<sub>0.44</sub>Mn<sub>0.95</sub>Ti<sub>0.05</sub>O<sub>2</sub>.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202407994-bib-0025" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202407994-bib-0025_R_d9131741e1622" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 25 - ACS Appl. Mater. Interfaces">25</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Compared with the deep etch XPS spectra of Ti 2p in Figures&nbsp;<a href="#adma202407994-fig-0003">3d,g</a> with peaks at 458 and 464.2&nbsp;eV corresponding to the Ti<sup>4+</sup> in the bulk, the surface of the deep etch XPS spectra of Ti 2p shows two additional weak peaks at 457 and 463&nbsp;eV, corresponding to Ti<sup>3+</sup> 2p3/2 and Ti<sup>3+</sup> 2p1/2, confirming the existence of the titanium-containing species.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202407994-bib-0026" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202407994-bib-0026_R_d9131741e1637" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 26 - Adv. Mater. ACS Appl. Energy Mater. ACS Appl. Mater. Interfaces">26</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> In addition, the contents of Mn and Ti show a gradual increase from the surface to the interior, showing a different structure between the inside and the outside, which may be responsible for the enhanced electrochemical properties. The deep etch XPS spectra of O 1&nbsp;s in Figures&nbsp;<a href="#adma202407994-fig-0003">3e,h</a> show that the oxygen defects in the bulk are surface lower than at the surface, which is not only because of the inevitable exposure to air but also as a result of the Ti─O bond reducing the oxygen defects in the bulk phase.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202407994-bib-0027" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202407994-bib-0027_R_d9131741e1645" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 27 - Small Nat. Commun. Angew. Chem., Int. Ed.">27</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup></p>
         
         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="adma202407994-fig-0003"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/2f9de20e-ec2c-4b0b-bc60-aadd9516f49a/adma202407994-fig-0003-m.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/2f9de20e-ec2c-4b0b-bc60-aadd9516f49a/adma202407994-fig-0003-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/512c3b61-277b-42aa-9c48-a028447cad60/adma202407994-fig-0003-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/2f9de20e-ec2c-4b0b-bc60-aadd9516f49a/adma202407994-fig-0003-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                  <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 3<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=adma202407994-fig-0003&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fadma.202407994" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                  </div>
                  <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">Crystal-structural evolution of Na<sub>0.44</sub>Mn<sub>0.95</sub>Ti<sub>0.05</sub>O<sub>2</sub> electrode (PVDF/NMP) during Na<sup>+</sup> extraction/insertion and surface valence analysis. a) In situ XRD pattern and corresponding charge/discharge curves of Na<sub>0.44</sub>Mn<sub>0.95</sub>Ti<sub>0.05</sub>O<sub>2</sub> electrode. b) Schematic diagram of crystal structure transformation during the charge and discharge process. XPS depth profile spectrum of c) Mn 2p d) Ti 2p and e) O 1s and corresponding intensity contour maps (bird's eye view) of f) Mn 2p g) Ti 2p and h) O 1s of Na<sub>0.44</sub>Mn<sub>0.95</sub>Ti<sub>0.05</sub>O<sub>2</sub>.</div>
               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
         <p>Large-scale practical applications of SIBs require cathode materials with excellent electrochemical performance, low cost, and environmental friendliness. Most of the current oxide cathodes show poor air/water stability and therefore require special storage and processing environments, which significantly increase the costs. In addition, the preparation of the oxide cathode slurry always involves the PVDF/NMP system, which is expensive and highly toxic, greatly increasing the difficulty of achieving large-scale application of oxide cathodes. Consequently, it is necessary to explore a way to improve the air/water stability of the oxide cathode for SIBs and avoid the use of organic solvents in the slurry process. Given the fact that Ti substituted materials possess excellent air stability. Here, the CMC/H<sub>2</sub>O system is used to investigate the feasibility of an aqueous slurry of Na<sub>0.44</sub>Mn<sub>1-x</sub>Ti<sub>x</sub>O<sub>2</sub> materials. CMC is a water-soluble polymer material, and the use of water as a solvent can avoid the toxicity generated by the use of organic solvents and reduce environmental pollution and safety hazards. Meanwhile, compared with the PVDF/NMP system, the cost of CMC and water is relatively low, which contributes to reducing the overall cost of battery manufacturing. As shown in <b>Figure</b>&nbsp;<a href="#adma202407994-fig-0004">4</a>, the electrochemical performance of the Na<sub>0.44</sub>Mn<sub>1-x</sub>Ti<sub>x</sub>O<sub>2</sub> cathode prepared with the CMC/H<sub>2</sub>O system is very similar to that of the PVDF/NMP system. However, as demonstrated by the initial five charge/discharge&nbsp;curves in Figures <a href="#adma202407994-fig-0004">4a–e</a> and the rate performance in Figures&nbsp;<a href="#adma202407994-fig-0004">4f–j</a> and Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S18</a> (Supporting Information), when the Ti substitution content is 0.15 (Na<sub>0.44</sub>Mn<sub>0.85</sub>Ti<sub>0.15</sub>O<sub>2</sub>), the cathode prepared with the CMC/H<sub>2</sub>O system shows the best performance, which is different from the optimal performance of the Na<sub>0.44</sub>Mn<sub>0.95</sub>Ti<sub>0.05</sub>O<sub>2</sub> cathode prepared with the PVDF/NMP system. Moreover, the GITT results in Figures <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S19,S20</a> (Supporting Information) also show that the Na<sub>0.44</sub>Mn<sub>0.85</sub>Ti<sub>0.15</sub>O<sub>2</sub> cathode prepared with CMC/H<sub>2</sub>O system displays good kinetic properties with minimal ohmic resistance compared to others. The suppressed Na<sup>+</sup>/vacancy ordering of the Na<sub>0.44</sub>MnO<sub>2</sub> with the CMC/H<sub>2</sub>O system can also be realized by Ti substitution, which is evidenced by the gradual smoothing of the CV curves with the increasing Ti substitution in Figures&nbsp;<a href="#adma202407994-fig-0004">4k–o</a>. In addition, according to the values of oxidation peaks of the CV curve of Na<sub>0.44</sub>Mn<sub>1-x</sub>Ti<sub>x</sub>O<sub>2</sub> materials at different scanning rates and the equation <i>i&nbsp;=&nbsp;av<sup>b</sup></i>, the b values are calculated to be 0.826, 0.9, 0.923, 0.883, and 0.893, respectively, which indicate that the Na<sub>0.44</sub>Mn<sub>1-x</sub>Ti<sub>x</sub>O<sub>2</sub> cathodes prepared with CMC/H<sub>2</sub>O system are also dominated by the capacitive sodium storage mechanism (Figures <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S21,S22</a>, Supporting Information). The Ti substitution Na<sub>0.44</sub>Mn<sub>1-x</sub>Ti<sub>x</sub>O<sub>2</sub> cathodes also possess excellent cycle stability even when prepared with a CMC/H<sub>2</sub>O system. As shown in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adma202407994-fig-0004">4p</a>, the optimal Na<sub>0.44</sub>Mn<sub>0.85</sub>Ti<sub>0.15</sub>O<sub>2</sub> shows a high capacity retention of 94.3% after 1000 cycles. Furthermore, the optimal Ti substitution amount of 0.15 in the Na<sub>0.44</sub>Mn<sub>1-x</sub>Ti<sub>x</sub>O<sub>2</sub> with CMC/H<sub>2</sub>O system was also confirmed by EIS of the cathode materials before and after cycle (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S23</a>, Supporting Information), where the pristine Na<sub>0.44</sub>Mn<sub>0.85</sub>Ti<sub>0.15</sub>O<sub>2</sub> sample shows the smallest charge transfer resistance and the Na<sub>0.44</sub>Mn<sub>0.8</sub>Ti<sub>0.2</sub>O<sub>2</sub> displays the lowest charge transfer resistance after cycle, which may be due to the activation of the epitaxial layer on the surface during the cycling process, contributing to the reduction of the cathode impedance. Hence, the incorporation of Ti significantly enhances the electrochemical and kinetic properties of the material compared to the pristine Na<sub>0.44</sub>MnO<sub>2</sub>. A comparative analysis of the electrochemical characteristics of Na<sub>0.44</sub>Mn<sub>1-x</sub>Ti<sub>x</sub>O<sub>2</sub> (0.05, 0.10, 0.15, 0.20) indicates that the material exhibits optimal comprehensive performance when x equals 0.15 (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S24</a>, Supporting Information). Meanwhile, the outstanding high-temperature electrochemical performance of the Na<sub>0.44</sub>Mn<sub>0.85</sub>Ti<sub>0.15</sub>O<sub>2</sub> cathode prepared with a CMC/H<sub>2</sub>O system was also convinced in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adma202407994-fig-0004">4q</a> and Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S25</a> (Supporting Information), which shows its superior cycle performance at 55&nbsp;°C with a capacity retention of 80.99% after 500 cycles at 2C.</p>
         
         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="adma202407994-fig-0004"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/942b6dc3-675a-4a35-b161-06ad2dcb6994/adma202407994-fig-0004-m.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/942b6dc3-675a-4a35-b161-06ad2dcb6994/adma202407994-fig-0004-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/15171877-6a66-40bc-8972-e87a83ad6632/adma202407994-fig-0004-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/942b6dc3-675a-4a35-b161-06ad2dcb6994/adma202407994-fig-0004-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                  <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 4<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=adma202407994-fig-0004&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fadma.202407994" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                  </div>
                  <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">Electrochemical performance of Na<sub>0.44</sub>Mn<sub>1-x</sub>Ti<sub>x</sub>O<sub>2</sub> (x&nbsp;=&nbsp;0, 0.05, 0.10, 0.15, 0.20) electrodes (CMC/H<sub>2</sub>O). a–e) Charge/discharge curves of Na<sub>0.44</sub>Mn<sub>1-x</sub>Ti<sub>x</sub>O<sub>2</sub> at 0.1C for the initial five cycles. f–j) Charge/discharge curves of Na<sub>0.44</sub>Mn<sub>1-x</sub>Ti<sub>x</sub>O<sub>2</sub> at different rates. k–o) CV of Na<sub>0.44</sub>Mn<sub>1-x</sub>Ti<sub>x</sub>O<sub>2</sub> at different scan rates. p) Cycle performance of Na<sub>0.44</sub>Mn<sub>1-x</sub>Ti<sub>x</sub>O<sub>2</sub> at 2C for 1000 cycles (after rate performance test). q) Rate and cycle performance of Na<sub>0.44</sub>Mn<sub>0.85</sub>Ti<sub>0.15</sub>O<sub>2</sub> at 55&nbsp;°C.</div>
               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
         <p>To reveal the phase transformation mechanism of the Na<sub>0.44</sub>MnO<sub>2</sub> and Na<sub>0.44</sub>Mn<sub>0.85</sub>Ti<sub>0.15</sub>O<sub>2</sub> cathode with CMC/H<sub>2</sub>O system, the in situ XRD was conducted during the initial charge/discharge process and its pattern and the correlation intensity local contours (bird's-eye view), as well as the schematic crystal structure, are shown in <b>Figures</b> <a href="#adma202407994-fig-0005">5a–d</a> and Figures <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S26,S27</a> (Supporting Information). Similar to the Ti substituted materials with PVDF/NMP system, the Na<sub>0.44</sub>Mn<sub>0.85</sub>Ti<sub>0.15</sub>O<sub>2</sub> cathode with CMC/H<sub>2</sub>O system also shows a reversible phase transition during the intercalation and extraction. During the charging process, the characteristic peaks (130), (140), (200), and (350) of the Na<sub>0.44</sub>Mn<sub>0.85</sub>Ti<sub>0.15</sub>O<sub>2</sub> gradually moved to a high angle and then returned to the initial position at the end of the discharging process. In addition, the (350) peak splits to generate a new (0 10 0) peak and disappears during the discharging process.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202407994-bib-0024" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202407994-bib-0024_R_d9131741e2018" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 24 - Chem. Eng. J.">24</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The new peak (010 0) derived from the (350) peak of Na<sub>0.44</sub>MnO<sub>2</sub> displays a greater shift toward a higher angle compared with Na<sub>0.44</sub>Mn<sub>0.85</sub>Ti<sub>0.15</sub>O<sub>2</sub>, which demonstrates that the Na<sub>0.44</sub>Mn<sub>0.85</sub>Ti<sub>0.15</sub>O<sub>2</sub> cathode prepared with CMC/H<sub>2</sub>O system still maintains excellent phase transition reversibility during the charge and discharge process. To explore the differences in the surface and bulk structure of Na<sub>0.44</sub>Mn<sub>0.85</sub>Ti<sub>0.15</sub>O<sub>2</sub> suitable for the CMC/H<sub>2</sub>O system, etched XPS was used to investigate the variations in the valence states of elements from the surface to the bulk (Figures&nbsp;<a href="#adma202407994-fig-0005">5e–g</a>; Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S28</a>, Supporting Information). The deep etch XPS spectra of Mn 2p show that the Mn<sup>4+</sup> content on the surface is higher than that of the bulk phase which can effectively inhibit the Jahn-Teller effect,<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202407994-bib-0028" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202407994-bib-0028_R_d9131741e2067" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 28 - Energy Storage Mater.">28</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> and the deep etch XPS spectra of Ti 2p display that the surface is enriched in Ti<sup>3+</sup>, demonstrating that the Ti substitution can generate an epitaxial layer containing Ti<sup>3+</sup> and this surface layer can protect the bulk structure, which may be the reason for the good electrochemical performance of the Na<sub>0.44</sub>Mn<sub>0.85</sub>Ti<sub>0.15</sub>O<sub>2</sub> with CMC/H<sub>2</sub>O system (Figures&nbsp;<a href="#adma202407994-fig-0005">5e,f</a>). In addition, the increase of Mn<sup>4+</sup> content on the surface may be due to the charge compensation effect caused by the Ti<sup>3+</sup> surface enrichment resulting from Ti substitution. Meanwhile, the presence of the surface protective layer containing Ti<sup>3+</sup> enhances the ability of Na<sub>0.44</sub>Mn<sub>0.85</sub>Ti<sub>0.15</sub>O<sub>2</sub> to resist air erosion, which can be inferred from the deep etch XPS spectra of Mn 2p with no obvious difference between the bulk and the surface (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adma202407994-fig-0005">5g</a>). Ex situ XPS characterization techniques to provide more information on the effect of Ti on the Mn valence state. Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S29</a> (Supporting Information) shows the XPS spectra of Mn 2p of Na<sub>0.44</sub>MnO<sub>2</sub>, Na<sub>0.44</sub>Mn<sub>0.95</sub>Ti<sub>0.05</sub>O<sub>2,</sub> and Na<sub>0.44</sub>Mn<sub>0.85</sub>Ti<sub>0.15</sub>O<sub>2</sub> electrodes (CMC/H<sub>2</sub>O) in different electrochemical states to further explore the change of Mn valence state. During charging up to 4.0&nbsp;V, the Mn 2p peaks were shifted toward higher binding energy, indicating that a considerable amount of Mn<sup>3+</sup> was oxidized to Mn<sup>4+</sup>. During discharge to 2.0&nbsp;V, the Mn 2p peak shifted toward lower binding energy.</p>
         
         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="adma202407994-fig-0005"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/bee02c4a-b513-4685-9240-381bc4f709a4/adma202407994-fig-0005-m.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/bee02c4a-b513-4685-9240-381bc4f709a4/adma202407994-fig-0005-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/480f292d-ca36-4704-ad24-c706a421ec95/adma202407994-fig-0005-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/bee02c4a-b513-4685-9240-381bc4f709a4/adma202407994-fig-0005-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                  <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 5<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=adma202407994-fig-0005&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fadma.202407994" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                  </div>
                  <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">Crystal-structural evolution of Na<sub>0.44</sub>Mn<sub>0.85</sub>Ti<sub>0.15</sub>O<sub>2</sub> electrode (CMC/H<sub>2</sub>O) during Na<sup>+</sup> extraction/insertion and surface valence analysis. a–c) In situ XRD pattern, corresponding charge/discharge curves, and local intensity contour plots (bird's-eye view) of Na<sub>0.44</sub>Mn<sub>0.85</sub>Ti<sub>0.15</sub>O<sub>2</sub> electrode. d) Schematic diagram of crystal structure transformation during the charge and discharge process. XPS depth profile spectrum of e) Mn 2p, f) Ti 2p, and g) O 1s.</div>
               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
         <p>Aiming at verifying the effect of the surface protective layer produced by Ti substitution on improving the air stability of materials, the air exposure experiment was carried out on Na<sub>0.44</sub>Mn<sub>0.85</sub>Ti<sub>0.15</sub>O<sub>2</sub> (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S30</a>, Supporting Information). The good air stability of oxide cathode materials for SIBs can significantly reduce the costs of production, storage, and transportation.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202407994-bib-0029" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202407994-bib-0029_R_d9131741e2196" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 29 - Adv. Energy Mater. Adv. Energy Mater.">29</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> As shown in <b>Figure</b> <a href="#adma202407994-fig-0006">6a</a>, the characteristic peaks in XRD patterns of the exposed sample show a slight positive shift compared to the pristine sample, and no new peaks corresponding to the impurity phase are generated, indicating the good structure stability of the Na<sub>0.44</sub>Mn<sub>0.85</sub>Ti<sub>0.15</sub>O<sub>2</sub> when exposed to air. Interestingly, the electrochemical performance of Na<sub>0.44</sub>Mn<sub>0.85</sub>Ti<sub>0.15</sub>O<sub>2</sub> exposed for three days is superior to the pristine Na<sub>0.44</sub>Mn<sub>0.85</sub>Ti<sub>0.15</sub>O<sub>2</sub> material, with better rate performance (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adma202407994-fig-0006">6b</a>), higher capacity (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adma202407994-fig-0006">6c</a>; Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S31</a>, Supporting Information) and cycle performance (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adma202407994-fig-0006">6d</a>), demonstrating that the Na<sub>0.44</sub>Mn<sub>0.85</sub>Ti<sub>0.15</sub>O<sub>2</sub> material has excellent air storage performance, which is beneficial to reducing the cost of its large-scale commercial production.</p>
         
         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="adma202407994-fig-0006"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/f01b49f7-e46a-4456-9d2b-0b148cb930a2/adma202407994-fig-0006-m.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/f01b49f7-e46a-4456-9d2b-0b148cb930a2/adma202407994-fig-0006-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/af074950-a190-4b73-9e22-f0bdaa436366/adma202407994-fig-0006-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/f01b49f7-e46a-4456-9d2b-0b148cb930a2/adma202407994-fig-0006-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                  <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 6<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=adma202407994-fig-0006&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fadma.202407994" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                  </div>
                  <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">Air stability of Na<sub>0.44</sub>Mn<sub>0.85</sub>Ti<sub>0.15</sub>O<sub>2</sub> material and electrochemical properties of industrial-grade Na<sub>0.44</sub>Mn<sub>0.85</sub>Ti<sub>0.15</sub>O<sub>2</sub> (Electrodes are manufactured with CMC binder). a) XRD patterns of Na<sub>0.44</sub>Mn<sub>0.85</sub>Ti<sub>0.15</sub>O<sub>2</sub> material exposed to air. b) Comparison of rates performance of Na<sub>0.44</sub>Mn<sub>0.85</sub>Ti<sub>0.15</sub>O<sub>2</sub> exposed to air for different days. c) Charge/discharge curves of Na<sub>0.44</sub>Mn<sub>0.85</sub>Ti<sub>0.15</sub>O<sub>2</sub> at different rates after three days of exposure to air. d) Exposure of air-exposed Na<sub>0.44</sub>Mn<sub>0.85</sub>Ti<sub>0.15</sub>O<sub>2</sub> for 1000 cycles at 2C (after rate performance test). e) The production process of industrial grade Na<sub>0.44</sub>Mn<sub>0.85</sub>Ti<sub>0.15</sub>O<sub>2</sub>. f) Charge/discharge curves of industrial-grade Na<sub>0.44</sub>Mn<sub>0.85</sub>Ti<sub>0.15</sub>O<sub>2</sub> at 0.1C for the initial five cycles. g) Charge/discharge curves of industrial-grade Na<sub>0.44</sub>Mn<sub>0.85</sub>Ti<sub>0.15</sub>O<sub>2</sub> at different rates. h) Rate and cycle performance of industrial-grade Na<sub>0.44</sub>Mn<sub>0.85</sub>Ti<sub>0.15</sub>O.</div>
               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
         <p>For the practical application of SIBs, it is very important to realize the preparation of cathode materials from laboratory scale to industrial scale. To verify the feasibility and superiority of the mass production of Na<sub>0.44</sub>Mn<sub>0.85</sub>Ti<sub>0.15</sub>O<sub>2</sub> material with CMC/H<sub>2</sub>O system, industrial-grade purity Na<sub>2</sub>CO<sub>3</sub>, Mn<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub>, and TiO<sub>2</sub> were used as raw materials to prepare the Na<sub>0.44</sub>Mn<sub>0.85</sub>Ti<sub>0.15</sub>O<sub>2</sub> material on a large scale. As shown in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adma202407994-fig-0006">6e</a>, the prepared amount of exceeding 10&nbsp;kg of Na<sub>0.44</sub>Mn<sub>0.85</sub>Ti<sub>0.15</sub>O<sub>2</sub> was successfully achieved, and it can be seen from the XRD pattern and SEM image in Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S32</a> (Supporting Information) that the large-scale prepared Na<sub>0.44</sub>Mn<sub>0.85</sub>Ti<sub>0.15</sub>O<sub>2</sub> from industrial-grade raw materials display the same crystal structure and tunnel morphology with the laboratory-grade analytical pure reagents. The electrochemical performance of the large-scale produced industrial-grade Na<sub>0.44</sub>Mn<sub>0.85</sub>Ti<sub>0.15</sub>O<sub>2</sub> cathode with CMC/H<sub>2</sub>O system is shown in Figures&nbsp;<a href="#adma202407994-fig-0006">6f–h</a>. The chage/discharge curves of industrial-grade Na<sub>0.44</sub>Mn<sub>0.85</sub>Ti<sub>0.15</sub>O<sub>2</sub> in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adma202407994-fig-0006">6f</a> shows smooth charging and discharging curves, which are very similar to the laboratory-grade counterpart. In addition, the industrial-grade Na<sub>0.44</sub>Mn<sub>0.85</sub>Ti<sub>0.15</sub>O<sub>2</sub> also exhibits a comparable rate and cycle performance with the laboratory-grade, the capacity retention rate of the industrial-grade Na<sub>0.44</sub>Mn<sub>0.85</sub>Ti<sub>0.15</sub>O<sub>2</sub> was still as high as 89.07% after 500 cycles at 1 C (Figures&nbsp;<a href="#adma202407994-fig-0006">6g,h</a>). In summary, the electrochemical performance of the industrial-grade Na<sub>0.44</sub>Mn<sub>0.85</sub>Ti<sub>0.15</sub>O<sub>2</sub> cathode material remains excellent, providing a new strategy for the development of practical industrial low-cost production of tunnel oxides.</p>
         
         <p>The assembly of a full cell requires a high sodium content in the cathode material, due to the inevitable and irreversible depletion of some Na ions by the solid electrolyte interphase (SEI) formed on the anode side during the initial charging process. Despite their excellent performance in half cells, tunnel Na<sub>0.44</sub>Mn<sub>1-x</sub>Ti<sub>x</sub>O<sub>2</sub> materials have rarely been reported for use as cathodes in full cells due to their naturally poor sodium. Therefore, it is very necessary to develop a sodium compensation technique for this material.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202407994-bib-0030" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202407994-bib-0030_R_d9131741e2482" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 30 - Adv. Mater.">30</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> As one of the cathode candidates for SIBs, Prussian blue analog (PBA) is rich in sodium. Herein, a strategy of introducing PBA into the tunnel oxide structure as a sodium compensating material to construct the PBA-Na<sub>0.44</sub>Mn<sub>0.85</sub>Ti<sub>0.15</sub>O<sub>2</sub> composite cathode was proposed. As the XRD results are shown in Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S33a</a> (Supporting Information), the PBA-Na<sub>0.44</sub>Mn<sub>0.85</sub>Ti<sub>0.15</sub>O<sub>2</sub> composite features both PBA and Na<sub>0.44</sub>Mn<sub>0.85</sub>Ti<sub>0.15</sub>O<sub>2</sub> characteristic peaks, indicating the successful preparation of the composite structure. The PBA-Na<sub>0.44</sub>Mn<sub>0.85</sub>Ti<sub>0.15</sub>O<sub>2</sub> composite cathode also displays excellent rate performance (<b>Figure</b> <a href="#adma202407994-fig-0007">7a-b</a>). In addition, the promising performance of the PBA-Na<sub>0.44</sub>Mn<sub>0.85</sub>Ti<sub>0.15</sub>O<sub>2</sub> composite cathode with CMC/H<sub>2</sub>O system was first validated in the half-cells, where Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adma202407994-fig-0007">7a</a> shows that the first charge capacity and the coulombic efficiency are greatly improved, because the PBA in the system, as shown in the CV curves in Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S33b</a> (Supporting Information), acted as complementary sodium source and offered the Fe<sup>2+</sup>/Fe<sup>3+</sup> redox couples to contribute the capacity and cycle performance with the capacity retention 70.61% after 1000 cycles at 2C (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adma202407994-fig-0007">7c</a>). To evaluate the practicality of the PBA-Na<sub>0.44</sub>Mn<sub>0.85</sub>Ti<sub>0.15</sub>O<sub>2</sub> composite cathode with the CMC/H<sub>2</sub>O system, a full cell was assembled as shown in the schematic of Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adma202407994-fig-0007">7d</a> using nonpresodiated hard carbon as the anode and 18650 type cylindrical battery was prepared and displayed in the photograph of Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adma202407994-fig-0007">7e</a>. The chage/discharge&nbsp;curves in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adma202407994-fig-0007">7f</a> show that the capacity of the coin full cell is 97.3&nbsp;mA&nbsp;h&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> for the first cycles at 0.1C, with an initial charge/discharge efficiency of 88.69% and the energy density of 300.4&nbsp;Wh&nbsp;kg<sup>−1</sup> (based on cathode active material) (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S34</a>, Supporting Information). In addition, the good rate and cycle performance of the coin full cell is shown in Figures&nbsp;<a href="#adma202407994-fig-0007">7g–i</a>, with a capacity retention rate of 67.36% at 0.5C for 300 cycles. 18650 type cylindrical batteries were assembled to further develop the PBA-Na<sub>0.44</sub>Mn<sub>0.85</sub>Ti<sub>0.15</sub>O<sub>2</sub> composite cathode toward practicality, delivering an initial discharge capacity of 654.2&nbsp;mA&nbsp;h with an initial charge/discharge efficiency of 81.78% at 0.1C (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adma202407994-fig-0007">7j</a>). In addition, the cylindrical battery also shows good rate performance with a capacity of 442.6&nbsp;mA&nbsp;h at 0.5C, and after the rate performance test, it still maintains good cycle&nbsp;performance, with a capacity retention rate of 78.54% after more than 130 cycles (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adma202407994-fig-0007">7k</a>). In summary, the cycle and rate performance of 18650 cylindrical batteries still need to be improved. Optimizing the whole process of cylindrical battery (such as slurry preparation, electrolyte selection, and diaphragm selection) is important to achieve remarkable performance and realize practical industrial applications of SIBs.</p>
         
         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="adma202407994-fig-0007"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/83da3e1b-0f66-47eb-ad39-21030e0bf1f7/adma202407994-fig-0007-m.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/83da3e1b-0f66-47eb-ad39-21030e0bf1f7/adma202407994-fig-0007-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/647f343c-1423-49bf-89fa-5048f4a3ea6b/adma202407994-fig-0007-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/83da3e1b-0f66-47eb-ad39-21030e0bf1f7/adma202407994-fig-0007-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                  <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 7<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=adma202407994-fig-0007&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fadma.202407994" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                  </div>
                  <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">The electrochemical characteristics of half-cells with PBA-Na<sub>0.44</sub>Mn<sub>0.85</sub>Ti<sub>0.15</sub>O<sub>2</sub> electrode (CMC/H<sub>2</sub>O) at 2.0–4.0&nbsp;V and the electrochemical performance of a full-cell system with industrial-grade PBA-Na<sub>0.44</sub>Mn<sub>0.85</sub>Ti<sub>0.15</sub>O<sub>2</sub> as the cathode and nonpresodiated hard carbon as the anode. a) Rate performance of PBA-Na<sub>0.44</sub>Mn<sub>0.85</sub>Ti<sub>0.15</sub>O<sub>2</sub>. b) Charge/discharge curves of PBA-Na<sub>0.44</sub>Mn<sub>0.85</sub>Ti<sub>0.15</sub>O<sub>2</sub> at different rates. c) Cycle performance of PBA-Na<sub>0.44</sub>Mn<sub>0.85</sub>Ti<sub>0.15</sub>O<sub>2</sub> for 1000 cycles at 2C (after rate performance test). d) Schematic diagram of PBA-Na<sub>0.44</sub>Mn<sub>0.85</sub>Ti<sub>0.15</sub>O<sub>2</sub> full cell. e) Photographs of the production of industrial-grade PBA-Na<sub>0.44</sub>Mn<sub>0.85</sub>Ti<sub>0.15</sub>O<sub>2</sub> electrode. f) Charge/discharge curves of coin full cell at 0.1C for initial five cycles. g) Rate performance of the coin full cell. h) Charge/discharge cycles of the coin full cell at different rates. i) Cycle performance of the coin full cell for 300 cycles at 0.5C (after rate performance test). j) Charge/discharge curves of 18650 batteries at 0.1C for the initial five cycles. k) Rate and cycle performance at 0.2C of 18650 batteries, and optical photograph of 18650 cylindrical batteries.</div>
               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
         <p>To go insight into the mechanism of improving the performance of Na<sub>0.44</sub>MnO<sub>2</sub> by Ti substitution, as shown in <b>Figures</b> <a href="#adma202407994-fig-0008">8a,b</a>, the models of Na<sub>0.44</sub>MnO<sub>2</sub> and Na<sub>0.44</sub>Mn<sub>0.85</sub>Ti<sub>0.15</sub>O<sub>2</sub> are constructed and calculated by DFT. In addition, DFT calculations were performed to simulate the embedding of Na ions during the discharge of Na<sub>0.44</sub>MnO<sub>2</sub> and Na<sub>0.44</sub>Mn<sub>0.85</sub>Ti<sub>0.15</sub>O<sub>2</sub> and to further investigate the effect of the Na<sup>+</sup>/vacancy disordered environment on the kinetics of Ti substitution. As shown in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adma202407994-fig-0008">8c</a>, when the Na ion was reinserted into the Na<sub>0.44</sub>MnO<sub>2</sub> and Na<sub>0.44</sub>Mn<sub>0.85</sub>Ti<sub>0.15</sub>O<sub>2</sub> with a Na-deficient state, the required anti-vacancy formation energy was −2.3219 and −3.5935&nbsp;eV, respectively, which indicates that the Na intercalation process of the Na<sub>0.44</sub>Mn<sub>0.85</sub>Ti<sub>0.15</sub>O<sub>2</sub> is a spontaneous reaction, suggesting the improved kinetics.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202407994-bib-0031" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202407994-bib-0031_R_d9131741e2751" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 31 - Nat. Energy Phys. Chem. Chem. Phys. Adv. Mater.">31</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The optimized structural models of Na<sub>0.44</sub>MnO<sub>2</sub> and Na<sub>0.44</sub>Mn<sub>0.85</sub>Ti<sub>0.15</sub>O<sub>2</sub> adsorbed by H<sub>2</sub>O molecule were constructed to perform DFT calculations to investigate the hydrophobicity of the prepared materials (Figures&nbsp;<a href="#adma202407994-fig-0008">8d–f</a>). It is known that negative values of E<sub>ads</sub> indicate spontaneous adsorption, whereas positive values of E<sub>ads</sub> do not lead to spontaneous adsorption.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202407994-bib-0032" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202407994-bib-0032_R_d9131741e2779" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 32 - Adv. Funct. Mater. ACS Nano ACS Catal.">32</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> As shown in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adma202407994-fig-0008">8d</a>, the adsorption energy of H<sub>2</sub>O on Na<sub>0.44</sub>MnO<sub>2</sub> is −0.0703&nbsp;eV, which is a spontaneous process, while the adsorption energy on Na<sub>0.44</sub>Mn<sub>0.85</sub>Ti<sub>0.15</sub>O<sub>2</sub> is 0.5725&nbsp;eV, demonstrating that the Ti-substituted Na<sub>0.44</sub>Mn<sub>0.85</sub>Ti<sub>0.15</sub>O<sub>2</sub> has good hydrophobicity. Therefore, the internal and external reinforcement strategy enhances the hydrophobicity and the Na<sup>+</sup> intercalation and extraction ability, which brings new vigor to the practical production application of Na<sub>0.44</sub>MnO<sub>2</sub> (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adma202407994-fig-0008">8g</a>).</p>
         
         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="adma202407994-fig-0008"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/78485ef2-f8d0-493d-98da-5d1b421f4b5b/adma202407994-fig-0008-m.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/78485ef2-f8d0-493d-98da-5d1b421f4b5b/adma202407994-fig-0008-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/cec9146f-f4f4-4fa3-82b7-e46ff0d4effb/adma202407994-fig-0008-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/78485ef2-f8d0-493d-98da-5d1b421f4b5b/adma202407994-fig-0008-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                  <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 8<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=adma202407994-fig-0008&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fadma.202407994" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                  </div>
                  <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">DFT calculations. Optimized structure of a) Na<sub>0.44</sub>MnO<sub>2</sub> and b) Na<sub>0.44</sub>Mn<sub>0.85</sub>Ti<sub>0.15</sub>O<sub>2</sub> with yellow atoms for Na, purple atoms for Mn, blue atoms for Ti, and red atoms for O. c) The anti-vacancy formation energy of one Na atom corresponded to Na<sub>0.44</sub>MnO<sub>2</sub> and Na<sub>0.44</sub>Mn<sub>0.85</sub>Ti<sub>0.15</sub>O<sub>2</sub>. d) The adsorption energy of Na<sub>0.44</sub>MnO<sub>2</sub> and Na<sub>0.44</sub>Mn<sub>0.85</sub>Ti<sub>0.15</sub>O<sub>2</sub> on H<sub>2</sub>O molecule. Structural diagram of e) Na<sub>0.44</sub>MnO<sub>2</sub> and f) Na<sub>0.44</sub>Mn<sub>0.85</sub>Ti<sub>0.15</sub>O<sub>2</sub> adsorbing one H<sub>2</sub>O molecule. g) Structural schematic of the mechanism effect of internal and external reinforcement strategy.</div>
               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
      </section>
      <section class="article-section__content" id="adma202407994-sec-0030">
         
         <h2 class="article-section__title section__title section1" id="adma202407994-sec-0030-title">3 Conclusion</h2>
         
         <p>In summary, this work adopts the internal and external synergistic enhancement strategy and the novel sodium compensation strategy for Na<sub>0.44</sub>MnO<sub>2</sub> cathode to achieve the industrialized application of coin full cell and 18650 battery. Under the guidance of DFT calculations, a series of characterization was conducted and proved that partially substituting Mn with Ti results in the optimized inner structure and formed the Ti epitaxial layer on the surface, which reduces the surface alkali, smoothes the charge/discharge curves and further improves the water resistance of the material. In addition, a novel sodium compensation strategy has been implemented to construct the PBA-Na<sub>0.44</sub>Mn<sub>0.85</sub>Ti<sub>0.15</sub>O<sub>2</sub> composite for industrial coin full cells and 18650 battery applications. This work has realized the large-scale production of tunnel oxides from laboratory to industrial scale for the first time, opening up the possibility of using SIBs in large-scale energy storage devices.</p>
         </section>
      <div class="article-section__content">
